Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
6 min
Diyah Payment Period: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on Killer's Own Wealth
Inter-madhhab dispute on diyah deferment from killer's own wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on diyah deferment, explain the Hanafi proof from qiyas, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
All diyah, even from the killer's own wealth, is deferred over three years in the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i: when a father deliberately kills his son, thus becoming personally liable for diyah, must he pay immediately or over three years? The answer hinges on the nature of diyah as an obligation contrary to qiyas (analogy) and the scope of the sharia's deferment. We will explore each school's evidence and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the case
Identify the scenario: a father deliberately kills his son, so qisas is waived (due to father-son relationship), and diyah becomes obligatory on the killer's own wealth. The dispute is whether this diyah is payable immediately or over three years.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Recall that the Hanafi school holds that all diyah, regardless of who pays, is deferred over three years. Their proof: diyah is an obligation of wealth for a life, which is contrary to qiyas (since life is not compensable by property). Since the sharia brought it as a deferred obligation, it must remain deferred and cannot be extended to immediate payment.
The key principle: something established contrary to qiyas is confined to its specific form.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that deferment is only for the 'aqila's ease. When the killer pays from his own wealth, there is no need for deferment; payment must be immediate. He views the deferment as a concession for the 'aqila, not a general rule.
4
Understand the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Hanafi father pays diyah in installments over three years; a Shafi'i father must pay the full amount immediately.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) within the school, supported by the principle of restricting a ruling that contradicts qiyas to its original application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کوئی باپ اپنے بیٹے کو عمدا قتل کر دے تو اس کی دیت کس طرح ہے اور کتنے دنوں میں وصول کی جائے گی
وما وجب على العاقلة من الدية او على القاتل بان قتل الاب ابنه عمدا فهو في ماله في ثلث سنين وقال الشافعى ما وجب على القاتل فى ماله فهو حال لان التاجيل للتخفيف لتحمل العاقلة فلا يلحق به العمد المحض
ترجمہ اور جو دیت کہ عاقلہ پر واجب ہے یا قاتل پر اس طریقے پر کہ باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کو عمدا قتل کیا ہو تو دیت قاتل کے مال میں ہو گی تین سالوں میں امام شافعی نے فرمایا جو دیت قاتل کے مال میں ہو وہ نقد ہوگی اس لئے کہ تا جیل تخفیف کی وجہ سے ہے عاقلہ کے تحمل کرنے کی وجہ سے تو عمد محض کو اسکے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جائیگا۔
تشریح امام ابو حنیفہ کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ دیت خواہ عاقلہ پر واجب ہو یا قاتل کے مال میں واجب ہو جیسے باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کو عمدا قتل کر دیا تو باپ پر دیت واجب ہے ، بہر حال ہمارے نزدیک جو بھی دیت ہو اس میں تا جیل ہے جو قسط وار تین سالوں میں ادا کی جائے گی ، امام شافعی یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جو دیت عاقلہ پر ہو وہ تو تین سالوں میں ادا کی جائے گی لیکن جو قتل عمد کی صورت میں کسی عارض کی وجہ سے دیت قاتل کے مال میں واجب ہوتی ہے اس میں تا جیل نہ ہوگی بلکہ وہ فی الحال واجب الاداء ہوگی کیونکہ عاقلہ بذات خود مجرم نہیں ہے تو اس پر تخفیف کی غرض دیت کی ادائے گی میں تا جیل مشروع ہوئی ہے تو قتل عمد محض کو اس کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
احناف کی دلیل
ولنا ان القياس يأباہ والشرع ورد به مؤجلا فلا يتعداه
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قیاس وجوب مال کا انکار کرتا ہے اور شریعت ایجاب مال کے ساتھ مال موجل کے ساتھ وارد ہوئی سے تو ایجاب مال تا جیل سے متعدی نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ نفس کے بدلہ میں مال واجب نہ ہوگا لیکن خلاف قیاس نفس سے ایجاب مال ثابت ہوا ہے جس کو دیت کہتے ہیں اور جو چیز خلاف قیاس ہوتی ہے اس کو مورد ساع سے بنانا جائز نہیں ہوتا اور شریعت میں جہاں بھی بطور دیت ایجاب مال مشروع ہوا ہے وہ موجل ہے اس کو بھی مؤجل ہی کہنا پڑے گا۔
If a father deliberately kills his son, what is the nature of his blood money and in how many days will it be collected? And what is obligatory upon the 'aqlah of blood money or upon the killer because the father killed his son deliberately, it is in his wealth in three years. Al-Shafi'i said: What is obligatory upon the killer in his wealth is immediate because deferment is for alleviation due to the burden of the 'aqlah, so pure intention cannot be attached to it. Translation: And the blood money that is obligatory upon the 'aqlah or upon the killer in the manner that the father deliberately killed his son, so the blood money will be in the killer's wealth in three years. Imam al-Shafi'i said: The blood money that is in the killer's wealth is cash because deferment is for alleviation due to the bearing of the 'aqlah, so pure intention will not be attached to it. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that blood money, whether obligatory upon the 'aqlah or in the killer's wealth, like a father who deliberately kills his son, the father is obligated to pay blood money; in any case, according to us, any blood money has deferment, which will be paid in installments over three years. Imam al-Shafi'i says: Blood money that is upon the 'aqlah will be paid in three years, but blood money that is obligatory in the killer's own wealth in a case of deliberate killing due to some impediment has no deferment; rather, it is immediately due because the 'aqlah itself is not criminal, so deferment was legislated to alleviate the payment of blood money, and pure deliberate killing cannot be attached to it. Our evidence: And we have that analogy rejects it, and the sharia came with it deferred, so it does not go beyond that. Translation: And our evidence is that analogy denies the obligation of wealth, and the sharia came with the obligation of wealth deferred, so the obligation of wealth will not go beyond deferment. Explanation: This is our evidence, the summary of which is that analogy required that wealth should not be obligatory in exchange for life, but contrary to analogy, the obligation of wealth from life has been established, which is called blood money, and something that is contrary to analogy cannot be made widespread, and wherever the sharia legislated the obligation of wealth as blood money, it is deferred, so this too must be considered deferred.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The issue is whether diyah (blood money) that becomes obligatory in the killer's own wealth (as in quasi-deliberate homicide by a father against his son) must be paid in installments over three years or immediately. The Hanafi position, held by Imam Abu Hanifa, is that all diyah, regardless of who pays, is deferred and paid over three years. The Hanafi evidence is that the obligation of property for a life is against qiyas (analogy), so it must be restricted to the specific way the sharia brought it—deferred. Imam al-Shafi'i argued that deferment is only for the 'aqila's benefit; when the killer pays from his own wealth, there is no need for ease, so payment should be immediate. The Hanafi rebuttal sticks to the principle that since diyah is established contrary to analogy, it cannot be extended beyond its original deferred form.

Key Terms
عاقلہ ('aqlah): The male agnatic relatives of the killer who are obligated to pay diyah in cases of accidental homicide.
تأجیل (ta'jil): Deferment of payment; specifically, paying diyah in installments over three years.
عمد محض (amd mahd): Pure deliberate intent to kill, without any impediment that would reduce the penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, over how many years is the diyah paid when a father deliberately kills his son?
A) Immediately
B) One year
C) Three years
D) Two years

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that all diyah is deferred over three years because it is an obligation contrary to qiyas and must remain in the form the sharia brought.

Diyat — Blood Money

Multiple Accidental Killers: Dividing Diyah Over Three Years
Ruling on multiple accidental killers and period starting from judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the diyah liability for multiple accidental killers and determine the start of the payment period.

Core Idea
When ten accidentally kill one, each pays one-tenth over three years starting from judgment, not the crime.

In accidental homicide, diyah is wajib on the killer or his 'aqila. But what if multiple persons jointly cause the death? The Hanafi school applies a clear qiyas (analogy) from a single killer to multiple killers, dividing the diyah proportionally. Additionally, a key detail is the starting point of the three-year payment period: it begins from the judge's verdict, not the date of the crime. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the precedent from walad al-maghroor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the hukm: if ten persons accidentally kill one, each owes one-tenth of the full diyah, payable over three years.
The diyah for accidental homicide is wajib.
2
Understand the qiyas
The ruling is derived by analogy from the single killer case: one killer pays full diyah over three years, so part (one-tenth) implies the same period.
The illa is that diyah is badal al-nafs (substitute for life), so liability is proportionate.
3
Trace the proof for timing
The three-year period starts from the judge's judgment (qada'), not from the crime. Reason: the original obligation is mithl (like property), and conversion to value (diyah) is by judgment.
Analogy: walad al-maghroor (child of a duped woman) where payment period is also from judgment.
4
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario of multiple accidental killers, determine each share and the deadline for payment.
Ensure the starting date is the verdict date.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر دس آدمیوں نے غلطی سے ایک شخص کو قتل کر دیا تو ہر ایک پر کتنی دیت ہوگی
ولو قتل عشرة رجلا خطأ فعلى كل واحد عشر الدية في ثلث سنين اعتباراً للجزء بالكل اذهو بدل النفس وانما يعتبر مدة ثلث سنين من وقت القضاء بالدية لان الواجب الاصلى المثل والتحول الى القيمة بالقضاء فيعتبر ابتداؤها من وقته كمافى ولد المغرور
ترجمہ اور اگر دس شخصوں نے ایک شخص کو خطاء قتل کر دیا ہو تو ہر ایک کے اوپر دیت کا عشر ہے تین سالوں کے اندر جزء کو کل پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اس لئے کہ یہ نفس کا بدل ہے اور تین سالوں کی مدت دیت کے فیصلہ کے وقت سے معتبر ہوگی اس لئے کہ واجب اصلی مثل ہے اور قیمت کی جانب تحول قضاء کی جانب ہے تو دیت کی ابتدا قضاء کے وقت سے معتبر ہوگی جیسے مغرور کے بچہ میں ۔
تشریح اگر دس آدمیوں نے خطا کسی ایک کو قتل کیا ہو تو ہر ایک پر دیت کا عشر واجب ہوگا جو ان سے تین سالوں میں وصول کیا جائے گا کیونکہ اگر وجوب ایک پر ہوتا تو ایسے ہی ہوتا لہذا اگر وجوب زیادہ پر ہوا ہے تب بھی ایسا ہی ہو گیا اور اس کی ادائے گی تین ہی سال میں کی جائے گی، کیونکہ یہ بہر حال نفس کا بدل اور عوض ہے اور اس کا متوجل ہو کر مشروع ہونا ابھی معلوم ہو چکا ہے۔ پھر قاضی کے فیصلہ دیت کے بعد جو تین سال آئیں گے ان میں دیت کو وصول کیا جائیگا کیونکہ اصل واجب تو مثل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ متلفات کا ضمان مثل سے ہوا کرتا ہے اور قیمت کی جانب تحول قضاء کی وجہ سے ہے تو دیت کی ابتدا قضاء کے وقت سے ہوگی جیسے ولد
And if ten men kill a man by mistake, then upon each one is one-tenth of the blood money in three years, considering the part by the whole because it is the substitute for the life. And the period of three years is considered from the time of the judgment regarding the blood money, because the original obligation is the like, and the conversion to value is by the judgment, so its beginning is considered from that time, as in the case of the child of the duped. Translation: And if ten persons kill one person by mistake, then upon each one is one-tenth of the blood money within three years, analogizing the part to the whole because this is the substitute for the life, and the period of three years will be considered from the time of the judgment of the blood money, because the original obligation is the like, and the conversion to value is by the judgment, so the beginning of the blood money will be considered from the time of the judgment, as in the child of the duped. Explanation: If ten men kill one by mistake, then each will owe one-tenth of the blood money, which will be collected from them over three years, because if the obligation were on one, it would be in the same way; similarly if the obligation is on many, it is the same. And its payment will be in three years, because it is in any case the substitute and recompense for life, and it has already been known that it is legislated as deferred. Then the three years that come after the judge's verdict regarding the blood money will be the time of collection, because the original obligation is like (similar goods), and conversion to value is by the judgment, so the beginning of the duty will be from the time of the judgment, like in the case of the child of the duped.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The Hanafi school states that if ten persons accidentally kill one person, each is liable for one-tenth of the diyah, and it must be paid in installments over three years. The reasoning is by analogy (qiyas) of the part to the whole: if one killer pays full diyah over three years, then each of multiple killers should pay his share over the same period. The proof also clarifies that the three-year period starts from the date of the judge's verdict, not from the date of the crime. This is because the original obligation is the mithl (the like, i.e., the same type of property), but since property may not be available, it is converted to value (price) by the judgment of the qadi. The analogy to walad al-maghroor (a child born by deception) is cited to support this timing.

Key Terms
بدل النفس (badal al-nafs): The substitute or recompense for a human life, i.e., diyah.
قضاء (qada'): The judge's final verdict or ruling regarding the payment of diyah.
ولد المغرور (walad al-maghroor): The case of a child born from a deceived woman; used as an analogy for starting period from judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the three-year period for paying diyah begin in a case of multiple accidental killers?
A) From the date of the crime
B) From the date of the judge's judgment
C) From the date of the first payment
D) From the date of arrest

Key Takeaway
In accidental homicide by multiple persons, each killer's diyah share is paid over three years starting from the judge's verdict, not the crime date.

Diyat — Blood Money

Ta'jil in Diyah: Universal Deferment vs. 'Aqila-Specific
Dispute on deferment of diyah: universal vs. 'āqila-specific

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on deferment of diyah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of restricting khilaf al-qiyas.

Core Idea
Diyah is deferred in all cases because it is a concession contrary to qiyās—concessions cannot be extended beyond their original scope.

This passage explores a key dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shāfi'ī regarding whether the deferment (ta'jīl) of diyah applies universally or only when the 'āqila pays. The Hanafis argue that diyah, being a concession contrary to analogical reasoning (qiyās), must be confined to the way the Sacred Law brought it—deferred over three years. Imam al-Shāfi'ī, however, restricts the concession to the 'āqila due to their lack of guilt. Understanding the principle behind this disagreement sharpens your ability to apply the rule that 'what is contrary to qiyās is limited to its textual scope.'

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that all diyah, whether on the 'āqila or on the killer (e.g., father killing son), is paid in installments over three years.
This is the muftā bihī position in the Hanafi school.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shāfi'ī holds that ta'jīl applies only when diyah is on the 'āqila; in cases where the killer pays (intentional killing with impediment), payment is immediate.
The Shafi'i dalil: the concession of deferment was legislated for the 'āqila because they are not direct aggressors.
3
Identify the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof is: 'Qiyās would refuse it, but the Sacred Law brought it deferred, so it cannot extend beyond deferment.' (al-qiyās ya'bāhu wa al-shar' warada bihi mu'ajjalan fa-lā yata'addāhu)
This is a dalil 'aqli (rational proof) based on the principle that rulings contrary to qiyās are restricted to their textual scope.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in a case of a father intentionally killing his son, Hanafis require deferred payment, Shafi'is require immediate payment.
The dispute hinges on whether the basis of ta'jīl is the nature of diyah as a concession or the identity of the payer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح امام ابو حنیفہ کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ دیت خواہ عاقلہ پر واجب ہو یا قاتل کے مال میں واجب ہو جیسے باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کو عمدا قتل کر دیا تو باپ پر دیت واجب ہے، بہر حال ہمارے نزدیک جو بھی دیت ہو اس میں تاجیل ہے جو قسط وار تین سالوں میں ادا کی جائے گی ، امام شافعی یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جودیت عاقلہ پر ہو وہ تو تین سالوں میں ادا کی جائے گی لیکن جو قتل عمد کی صورت میں کسی عارض کی وجہ سے دیت قاتل کے مال میں واجب ہوتی ہے اس میں تاجیل نہ ہوگی بلکہ وہ فی الحال واجب الاداء ہوگی کیونکہ عاقلہ بذات خود مجرم نہیں ہے تو اس پر تخفیف کی غرض دیت کی ادائے گی میں تا جیل مشروع ہوئی ہے تو قتل عمد محض کو اس کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
احناف کی دلیل
ولنا ان القياس يأباة والشرع ورد به مؤجلا فلا يتعداه
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قیاس وجوب مال کا انکار کرتا ہے اور شریعت ایجاب مال کے ساتھ مال موجل کے ساتھ وارد ہوئی سے تو ایجاب مال تا جیل سے متعدی نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ نفس کے بدلہ میں مال واجب نہ ہوگا لیکن خلاف قیاس نفس سے ایجاب مال ثابت ہوا ہے جس کو دیت کہتے ہیں اور جو چیز خلاف قیاس ہوتی ہے اس کو مورد ساع سے بنانا جائز نہیں ہوتا اور شریعت میں جہاں بھی بطور دیت ایجاب مال مشروع ہوا ہے وہ موجل ہے اس کو بھی مؤجل ہی کہنا پڑے گا۔
Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that dīyah, whether obligatory on the 'āqila or on the killer's wealth — such as when a father intentionally kills his son, so dīyah is obligatory on the father — in any case, according to us, any dīyah has deferment (ta'jīl) and will be paid in installments over three years. Imam al-Shāfi'ī says: That dīyah which is upon the 'āqila will be paid over three years, but in the case of intentional killing when dīyah becomes obligatory on the killer's wealth due to some impediment, there is no deferment; rather it is immediately due because the 'āqila is not itself a criminal, so deferment was legislated for them as a concession, so pure intentional killing cannot be annexed to it. Proof of the Hanafis: 'We have that analogical reasoning (qiyās) opposes it, and the Sacred Law has brought it deferred, so it does not extend beyond that.' Translation: And our proof is that qiyās denies the imposition of wealth, and the Sacred Law came with the imposition of wealth as deferred, so the imposition of wealth will not extend beyond deferment. Explanation: This is our proof, the gist of which is that qiyās would require that wealth not be obligatory in exchange for a life, but contrary to qiyās, the imposition of wealth (dīyah) for a life is established, and what is contrary to qiyās cannot be extended beyond its textual scope, and wherever the Sacred Law has legislated the imposition of wealth as dīyah, it is deferred; hence this must also be deferred.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shāfi'ī regarding whether the deferment (ta'jīl) of dīyah applies universally or only when it is on the 'āqila. The author first states the Hanafi position: all dīyah, whether on the 'āqila or on the killer (e.g., when the father kills his son), is paid in installments over three years. Then he presents Imam al-Shāfi'ī's view: only dīyah on the 'āqila is deferred; dīyah on the killer's own wealth in intentional killing is immediately due because the concession of deferment was given to the 'āqila who are not direct aggressors. The Hanafi proof is given in Arabic: 'Qiyās would refuse it (i.e., no property liability for a life), but the Sacred Law came with it as deferred, so it cannot extend beyond (the deferment).' The commentary explains that since dīyah is a concession contrary to qiyās, it must be confined to the way the Law brought it—deferred. Therefore, even when the liability shifts to the killer (due to impediments like father killing son), the deferment remains.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (ʿāqila): The kinship group or tribe liable to pay dīyah on behalf of a member who commits homicide.
دیت (dīyah): Financial compensation paid to the heirs of a homicide victim.
تاجیل (ta'jīl): Deferment or payment in installments over a period (here three years).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a father intentionally kills his son, how is the dīyah paid?
A) Immediately, because it is intentional
B) Over three years in installments
C) Not paid because the father is the heir
D) Paid by the tribe in one lump sum

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule on ta'jīl of diyah exemplifies the principle that rulings contrary to qiyās are confined to their textual scope — deferment applies universally.

Diyah for Ten Killers in Khata'
Ruling on multiple unintentional killers each paying one-tenth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that multiple unintentional killers divide the diyah proportionally, with payment starting from the judge's verdict.

Core Idea
Ten killers share the diyah: each pays one-tenth over three years from judgment.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: when ten people unintentionally cause a single death, the financial compensation (diyah) is divided among them. Each pays one-tenth of the full diyah, and the three-year payment period begins from the judge's verdict, not from the time of death. The ruling is derived by analogy (qiyas) to the case of a single killer and is supported by the broader principle that the original obligation is a specific substitute (mithl) that converts to value upon judgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the ruling
The text states that ten persons kill one man by mistake (khata'). The ruling: each killer must pay one-tenth of the full diyah.
Note that the full diyah is the amount owed by a single unintentional killer.
2
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The ruling is derived by comparing the multiple-killer case to the single-killer case. Just as one killer pays full diyah, ten killers share that obligation proportionally. The illa (effective cause) is that diyah is a substitute for the life (badal al-nafs), which can be divided when liability is shared.
This is a clear qiyas jaliy (obvious analogy).
3
Determine the payment period
The diyah is payable over three years. The text clarifies that the three years are counted from the time of the judge's verdict (qada'), not from the death. This is because the original obligation is the like (mithl), which converts to a monetary value only upon judgment.
If the period started from death, the killers might have to pay before the judgment, which is not practical.
4
Recognize the supporting analogy with walad al-maghrur
The author cites the case of the child of a deceived woman (maghrur) as a parallel: the value of the child is assessed at the date of judgment, not the date of birth. Similarly, the diyah period begins at judgment.
This reinforces the principle that when an obligation converts from mithl to value, the starting point is the judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قتل عشرة رجلا خطأ فعلى كل واحد عشر الدية في ثلث سنين اعتباراً للجزء بالكل اذهو بدل النفس وانما يعتبر مدة ثلث سنين من وقت القضاء بالدية لان الواجب الاصلى المثل والتحول الى القيمة بالقضاء فيعتبر ابتداؤها من وقته كمافى ولد المغرور

And if ten persons kill a man by mistake, then upon each one is one-tenth of the diyah in three years, considering the part by analogy to the whole, because it is the substitute for a life. And the period of three years is considered from the time of the judgment (qaḍā') regarding the diyah, because the original obligation is the like (mithl), and the conversion to value is by judgment, so its beginning is considered from that time, as in the case of the child of the deceived woman (walad al-maghrūr). Translation: And if ten persons killed a person by mistake, then on each one is one-tenth of the diyah within three years, drawing an analogy of the part to the whole. This is because it is the substitute for the life, and the period of three years will be considered from the time of the judgment of diyah, because the original obligation is the like, and the conversion to value is by judgment, so the beginning of the diyah will be considered from the time of judgment, like in the case of the deceived woman's child. Explanation: If ten persons mistakenly killed one person, then on each one is obligatory one-tenth of the diyah, which will be collected from them over three years. Because if the obligation were on one, it would be the same; hence if the obligation falls on many, it is also the same, and its payment will be made in three years. This is because it is the substitute and compensation for a life, and it has become clear that it is legislated as deferred. Then the diyah will be collected in the three years following the judge's verdict, because the original obligation is the like, as the guarantee for damaged property is by the like, and the conversion to value is due to judgment, so the beginning of the diyah will be from the time of judgment, as in the case of the child of the deceived woman: for example, a woman married a man, and she had told him that she was free; so some children were born, and someone claimed that this woman is his slave-girl; then that slave-girl will be returned to the claimant, and her children will be free, but their value must be paid. And the value is considered from the day of judgment. Similarly, here the period begins from the time of judgment.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof: when ten people kill one person by mistake, each pays one-tenth of the full diyah, and they pay over three years. The proof is that the whole (full diyah for one killer) is divided analogously (qiyās). The author then addresses a secondary issue: the three-year period begins from the judge's verdict, not from the death. This is because the original obligation (mithl) is a specific substitute, but when it converts to value (by judgment), the timing starts from that judgment. The commentary illustrates this with the analogy of the child of a deceived woman (maghrūr), where the value is determined at the date of judgment.

Key Terms
دیت (dīyah): Financial compensation for homicide.
مثل (mithl): The like or equivalent; here referring to the original obligation of a specific substitute (e.g., a specific number of camels).
قضاء (qaḍā'): The judge's verdict or court judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When multiple people unintentionally kill one person, each pays a proportional share of the diyah over three years starting from the judge's verdict.

Determining the 'Āqila for Non-Diwān Persons
Ruling on 'āqila for non-dīwān persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the 'āqila of a non-dīwān person and explain the legal basis of nuṣrah.

Core Idea
Your 'āqila is your support network: tribe for civilians, state for soldiers.

In Hanafi fiqh, the 'āqila (the group liable for dīyah) varies based on a person's affiliation. Al-Qudūrī clarifies that for those not enrolled in the state dīwān (military roll), their 'āqila is their tribe (qabīlah), because 'āqila liability hinges on mutual assistance (nuṣrah). This ruling ensures that every Muslim has a responsible group to share blood money liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Determine whether the person is from the ahl al-dīwān (those registered in the military/state register). The ruling applies when the person is NOT from the dīwān.
The dīwān typically includes soldiers and state employees entitled to stipends.
2
State the ruling
If the person is not from the dīwān, then his 'āqila is his tribe (qabīlah). The tribe includes extended family who would naturally support him.
The tribe is the primary group for civilians.
3
Identify the rationale (ʿillah)
The basis for 'āqila is nuṣrah (mutual assistance). For a non-diwān person, his support comes from his tribe, so they are his 'āqila.
Nuṣrah is the operative cause that determines liability.
4
Contrast with dīwān persons
For those registered in the dīwān, the 'āqila is the state or army because their support comes from that system. This ruling only covers non-diwān persons.
The opposite case is governed by a different ruling (not in this passage).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن يكن من اهل الديوان فعاقلته قبيلته لان نصرته بهم وهي المعتبرة في التعاقل
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جو اہل دیوان میں سے نہ ہو تو اسکا عاقلہ اس کا قبیلہ ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی نصرت انہیں کی وجہ سے ہے اور عاقلہ ہونے میں نصرت ہی معتبر ہے۔
تشریح اگر کوئی اہل دیوان میں سے نہ ہو تو اس کے عاقلہ اس کا قبیلہ اور اس کا خاندان ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس کے بعد گا ر اس کا خاندان ہوتا ہے اور نصرت ہی کی بنیاد پر عاقلہ ہونے کا مدار ہے۔
He (al-Qudūrī) said: And whoever is not from the people of the dīwān, then his 'āqila is his tribe (qabīlah), because his assistance (nuṣrah) is from them, and that (assistance) is what is considered in 'āqila liability. Translation: Al-Qudūrī said: And whoever is not from the people of the dīwān, his 'āqila is his tribe, because his assistance is through them, and in being an 'āqila, assistance alone is considered. Explanation: If someone is not from the people of the dīwān, then his 'āqila is his tribe and his family, because his backing is his family, and the basis for being an 'āqila is assistance.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Qudūrī, stating that for a person who does not belong to the dīwān (the military/state register), his 'āqila is his tribe (qabīlah). The reasoning given is that 'āqila liability is based on mutual assistance (nuṣrah), and for someone not in the dīwān, his support comes from his tribe. The commentary reiterates that the basis for 'āqila is the capacity to provide help, and for a non-diwan person, that is the family/tribe.

Key Terms
دیوان (dīwān): The military or state register of persons entitled to stipends, often soldiers.
عاقلہ (ʿāqila): The group liable to pay dīyah.
قبیلہ (qabīlah): Tribe or extended family.
نصرت (nuṣrah): Mutual assistance or support.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For a non-dīwān person, the 'āqila is his tribe because mutual assistance (nuṣrah) determines liability.

The Maximum Annual Payment from Each Member of 'Āqila
Intra-Hanafi dispute on maximum per-person diyah payment over three years

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Muhammad's position on the maximum total dirhams each 'āqila member pays over three years and explain why it is deemed aṣaḥḥ.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad: each 'āqila member pays at most 3–4 dirhams total over three years; al-Qudūrī's allowance of 4 per year is not operative.

This passage addresses a practical point: when diyah is distributed among the 'āqila (tribal group), how much can each member be required to pay annually? Al-Qudūrī's text appears to allow up to 4 dirhams per year, but Imam Muhammad explicitly caps the total over the three-year period at 3 or 4 dirhams. The commentary clarifies that Imam Muhammad's ruling is the most correct (aṣaḥḥ), preventing excessive burden on the 'āqila members.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate al-Qudūrī's statement in the text: 'لا يزاد الواحد على اربعة دراهم فى كل سنة' (no one is charged more than four dirhams each year). Then note Imam Muhammad's explicit ruling: 'لا يزاد على كل واحد من جميع الدية فى ثلث سنين على ثلثة او اربعة' (no one is charged more than three or four from the total over three years).
Al-Qudūrī's text is from his Mukhtasar; Imam Muhammad's is from his own works (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah).
2
Understand the implication of each
Al-Qudūrī's statement could be read as allowing up to 4 dirhams per year, which would total 12 dirhams over three years. Imam Muhammad explicitly limits the total to 3 or 4 dirhams, equating to 1 or 1⅓ dirhams per year.
The difference is significant: 12 vs. 3-4 dirhams total.
3
Note the author's tarjih
The commentary declares 'هو الاصح' (it is the most correct) after presenting Imam Muhammad's view, indicating that Imam Muhammad's position is the preferred (muftā bihī) ruling.
The tarjih is based on the authority of Imam Muhammad and the principle of not overburdening the 'āqila.
4
Apply the ruling
From Imam Muhammad's limit, the practical annual payment is either 1 dirham per year (total 3) or 1⅓ dirhams per year (total 4), depending on the need.
Reduction below this is permissible, but increase is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتقسم عليهم في ثلث سنين لا يزاد الواحد على اربعة دراهم فى كل سنة وينقص منها قال رضى الله عنه كذا ذكره القدورى فى مختصره وهذا اشارة الى انه يزاد على اربعة من جميع الدية وقد نص محمد على انه لا يزاد على كل واحد من جميع الدية فى ثلث سنين على ثلثة او اربعة فلا يؤخذ من كل واحد في كل سنة الادرهما او درهما وثلث درهم وهو الاصح
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور دیت کو قبیلہ پر تین سالوں میں تقسیم کر دیا جائیگا ہر سال میں ایک سے چار درہموں سے زیادہ نہیں لیا جائے گا اور اس سے کم کیا جا سکتا ہے ، مصنف نے فرمایا کہ قدوری نے اپنی مختصر میں یونہی ذکر کیا ہے اور یہ اس بات کی جانب اشارہ ہے کہ پوری دیت میں چار سے بڑھایا جا سکتا ہے حالانکہ امام محمد نے صراحت کی ہے کہ ایک پر پوری دیت میں تین سالوں کے اندر تین یا چار درہموں پر بڑھا یا نہیں جائے گا تو ہر سال میں ہر ایک سے صرف ایک درہم یا ایک درہم اور ایک درہم کا ( ) لیا جائے گا اور یہی اصح ہے۔
تشریح جب قبیلہ والوں پر دیت کو تقسیم کیا جائے تو اس میں یہ خیال رہے گا کہ پوری دیت ان سے تین سال میں قسط وار وصول ہوگی اور سالانہ ہر ایک سے صرف ایک درہم لیا جائے تا کہ مجموعہ تین ہو جائے یا ہر ایک سے ایک درہم اور درہم کا تہائی لیا جائے تا کہ مجموعہ چار در اہم ہو جائے کیونکہ کسی سے چار سے زیادہ لینا جائز نہیں ہے اگر چہ کم کر دینے کی گنجائش ہے لیکن زیادتی کی نہیں ہے۔ امام قدوری کا کلام سامنے ہے اس سے بظاہر یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تین سال میں ہر ایک سے چار درہموں سے زیادہ کیا جا سکتا ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے یہ فرمایا ہے کہ کسی سے سالانہ چار سے زیادہ نہیں لئے جا سکتے البتہ چار سے کم کئے جاسکتے ہیں اور یہ امام محمد کی تصریح کے خلاف سے اور اسح وہی سے جو امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے۔
He said: And it is divided among them (the tribe) over three years; no one is charged more than four dirhams in each year, and it may be reduced from that. The author (Radi Allah 'anhu) said: Thus al-Qudūrī mentioned it in his Mukhtasar, and this is an indication that it may be increased beyond four from the total diyah, even though Muhammad (al-Shaybānī) explicitly stated that no one is charged more than three or four from the total diyah over three years; thus each person in each year may be charged only two dirhams or one and a third dirham, and this is the most correct (aṣaḥḥ). Translation: Al-Qudūrī said: And the diyah is divided among the tribe over three years; from one person no more than four dirhams may be taken in each year, and less may be taken. The author said that al-Qudūrī mentioned thus in his Mukhtasar, and this indicates that it can be increased beyond four from the entire diyah, whereas Imam Muhammad explicitly stated that one may not be charged more than three or four from the total diyah over three years; so from each person in each year only one dirham or one and one-third dirhams will be taken, and this is the most correct. Explanation: When the diyah is divided among the tribe, it should be observed that the entire diyah will be collected from them over three years in installments, and annually from each person only one dirham is taken so that the total becomes three, or from each one dirham and one-third dirham is taken so that the total becomes four dirhams. Because taking more than four from anyone is not permissible, although reduction is allowed, but increase is not. Imam al-Qudūrī's statement suggests that over three years, more than four dirhams can be taken per person per year? Actually his words only say no more than four per year, but the author interprets that as implying increase from the total? The correct position is Imam Muhammad's: a total of three or four dirhams over three years, meaning one or one and a third per year.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding how much each member of the 'āqila pays annually towards the diyah. Al-Qudūrī's text states that in each year, no one is charged more than four dirhams, but less is allowed. The author (of the commentary) interprets this as permitting an increase beyond four dirhams per year from the total diyah (i.e., if the total sum requires it). However, Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybānī) explicitly states that over the three years, each person's total contribution should not exceed three or four dirhams—meaning only one dirham per year (total 3) or one and a third per year (total 4). The commentary clarifies that Imam Muhammad's view is the most correct (aṣaḥḥ). The lower limit prevents overburdening the 'āqila members. The author notes that Qudūrī's wording might be misunderstood, but the relied-upon position is that of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms
درہم (dirham): A silver coin, the basic unit of currency in this context.
اصح (aṣaḥḥ): The most correct opinion among the Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of the commentary, which view is declared 'aṣaḥḥ'?
A) Al-Qudūrī's view
B) Imam Muhammad's view
C) Both views are equally correct
D) Neither view is correct

Key Takeaway
The muftā bihī in the Hanafi school is that each 'āqila member pays at most one dirham or one and one-third dirhams per year over three years.

Supplementing the 'Aqila: Adding the Closest Tribe
Ruling on expanding 'aqila with closest tribe

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplementing the 'aqila when it is insufficient for diyah, and identify the order of additional tribes based on the hierarchy of 'asabat.

Core Idea
When the 'aqila cannot pay, the next agnatic tribe is added in the order of 'asabat.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses a practical scenario in diyah (blood money) law: what happens when the 'aqila tribe lacks the resources to pay the full diyah? The Hanafi school provides a clear mechanism to supplement the 'aqila by adding the closest tribe in lineage, following the same order as 'asabat (agnatic heirs). This ruling is rooted in the principle of alleviation (takhfif) to prevent undue burden on individuals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the condition: the 'aqila tribe (male agnatic relatives) is insufficient to pay the full diyah for unintentional homicide.
The insufficiency could be due to small size or poverty.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that the next closest tribe in lineage is annexed (ضم) to the original 'aqila to collectively pay the diyah.
This is based on the matn of al-Quduri: 'ضم اليهم اقرب القبائل'.
3
Explain the rationale (takhfif)
The obligation of diyah on the 'aqila is for alleviation (تخفيف), so that no individual pays more than a small amount (about 4 dirhams). Adding the closest tribe spreads the burden further.
Takhfif is the underlying cause (illah) for making the 'aqila liable.
4
Determine the order of addition
Tribes are added in the order of the closest then the next closest, following the sequence of 'asabat: brothers, then their sons, then paternal uncles, then their sons, and so on.
This order mirrors inheritance hierarchy for residuaries.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that each member of the 'aqila pays an equal amount (half a dinar) regardless of closeness, whereas Hanafis prioritize lineage proximity.
This difference affects distribution, not obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عاقلہ کا قبیلہ ادائیگی دیت کے لئے ناکافی ہو تو دوسرا قبیلہ جو نسبا قریب ہوا سے دیت میں شامل کیا جائے گا
كتاب المعاقل
قال وان لم يكن تتسع القبيلة لذلك ضم اليهم اقرب القبائل معناه نسبا كل ذلك لمعنى التخفيف ويضم الاقرب فالاقرب على ترتيب العصبات الاخوة ثم بنوهم ثم الأعمام ثم بنوه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر قبیلہ اس کے لئے وسیع نہ ہو تو باعتبار نسب اقرب القبائل کو ان کی طرف ملا دیا جائے یہ تمام باتیں تخفیف کی وجہ سے ہیں اور اقرب فالا قرب کو ملایا جائے عصبات کی ترتیب کے مطابق بھائیوں کو پھر بھتیجوں کو پھر چچاؤں کو پھر ان کے بیٹوں کو۔
تشریح جس قبیلہ کو اس کا عاقلہ شمار کیا گیا تھا وہ اداء دیت کے لئے ناکافی ہے، تو دوسرا وہ قبیلہ ان کی طرف ملا دیا جائے گا جو نسب کے اعتبار سے ان کے قریب ہو اس لئے کہ عاقلہ پر دیت کا وجوب تخفیف کی غرض سے ہے اور تخفیف اس میں ہے جو ہم نے بتایا کہ ایک شخص پر پوری دیت کے اندر چار درہم سے زیادہ نہ ہونے پائیں لہذا الا قرب فالا قرب کے لحاظ سے قبائل کو ملا دیا جائے گا اور الا قرب فالا قرب کی وہی ترتیب ہے جو عصبات کی ترتیب ہے یعنی اولا قاتل کے بھائیوں کو ملایا جائے گا پھر بھائیوں کے بیٹوں کو پھر چچاؤں کو پھر چچا زاد بھائیوں کو۔ (وقد بين ترتيب العصبات مفصلاً في درس السراجي)۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And if the tribe is not sufficient for that, then the closest tribes in lineage are annexed to them, all for the meaning of alleviation. And the closest then the next closest are annexed according to the order of 'asabat: the brothers, then their sons, then the paternal uncles, then their sons. Commentary: The tribe that was considered his 'aqila is insufficient for payment of diyah, so another tribe that is closer in lineage is annexed to them, because the obligation of diyah on the 'aqila is for alleviation, and the alleviation is that no person bears more than four dirhams from the full diyah. So tribes are annexed considering the closest then the next closest, and the order of the closest then the next closest is the same as the order of 'asabat: first the killer's brothers are annexed, then their sons, then the paternal uncles, then the sons of paternal uncles. (The order of 'asabat has been detailed in the lesson on al-Sirajiyyah).
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Quduri with expansion. It addresses the scenario where the 'aqila tribe is insufficient to pay the full diyah (blood money). The ruling is that the next closest tribe in lineage is added to the 'aqila. This is based on the principle of takhfif (alleviation), which is the underlying reason for making the 'aqila liable in the first place. The order of adding follows the same hierarchy as 'asabat (agnatic heirs): brothers, then their sons, then paternal uncles, then their sons. The commentator emphasizes that this alleviation ensures that no individual member pays more than three or four dirhams. The reference to al-Sirajiyyah indicates that the detailed order of 'asabat is well-known in inheritance law.

Key Terms
عاقلہ ('aqila): The group of male agnatic relatives (tribe) who are collectively responsible for paying diyah on behalf of one of their members who has committed unintentional homicide.
عصبات ('asabat): Agnatic relatives who inherit as residuaries. Their order is used here to determine the sequence of adding tribes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The tribe with the most members
B) The tribe that is closest in lineage following the order of 'asabat
C) The tribe of the mother's relatives
D) The tribe that the imam arbitrarily chooses

Key Takeaway
When the 'aqila is insufficient, the next agnatic tribe is added in the order of 'asabat to fulfill the diyah.

Including the Killer's Father and Sons in the 'Aqila: A Hanafi Dispute
Internal Hanafi dispute on 'aqila membership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi opinions on including the killer's father and sons in the 'aqila and explain the rationale (closeness vs. multiplicity) for each.

Core Idea
The killer's father and sons: too close to include, or too few to help? A Hanafi divide.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi difference concerning the composition of the 'aqila. The dispute turns on the underlying rationale of the 'aqila system: is it based on proximity and support (qarabah) or on distributing the burden among many (kathrah)? Two valid opinions emerge within the school, both rooted in the same objective of alleviating hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opinions
Read the passage and pinpoint the two positions: one includes the killer's father and sons (asa and abnai) in the 'aqila, the other excludes them.
Both opinions are introduced with 'قيل' (it is said) without naming specific imams.
2
Analyse the rationale for inclusion
The first opinion argues that they are included due to their closeness (qurbah). Since the 'aqila is based on support and proximity, the closest relatives are the most natural candidates.
This view prioritises lineage nearness as the core principle.
3
Analyse the rationale for exclusion
The second opinion argues that the purpose of annexing others to the 'aqila (ضم) is to remove hardship (nafy al-haraj) by distributing the diyah payment among many people, so that each pays no more than three or four dirhams. Fathers and sons are typically few, so including them would not achieve this distribution.
This view prioritises the functional purpose of the 'aqila over mere closeness.
4
Recognise the unresolved nature
The passage does not give preference to either opinion. Both are presented as valid within the Hanafi school, leaving the matter as a recognised ikhtilaf.
A mufti may choose either view depending on circumstances, though some later works may give preference.
5
Apply the dispute to a practical scenario
Consider a case: The killer's father and adult sons are alive. If the first opinion is followed, they must contribute to the diyah. If the second is followed, they are exempt. The difference directly affects their financial liability.
This thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) matters in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما الاباء والابناء فقيل يدخلون لقربهم وقيل لا يدخلون لأن الضم لنفى الحرج حتى لا يصيب كل واحد اكثر من ثلثة او اربعة وهذا المعنى انما يتحقق عند الكثرة والاباء والابناء لا يكثرون
ترجمہ اور بہر حال آباء اور ابنا ء پس کہا گیا ہے کہ وہ عاقلہ میں داخل ہوں گے ان کے قرب کی وجہ سے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ داخل نہ ہوں گے اس لئے کہ ضم جرح کو دور کرنے کے لئے ہے تا کہ ہر ایک کو تین یا چار سے زیادہ نہ پہنچے اور یہ معنی کثرت کے وقت متحقق ہوتے ہیں اور آباء اور ابنا، کثیر نہیں ہوتے ۔ تشریح یہاں یہ سوال ہے کہ عا قالہ کی فہرست میں قاتل کے آبا ، اور اس کے بیٹے بھی داخل ہیں یا نہیں تو یہاں دو قول ہیں ا جب عاقلہ ہونے کی بنیاد نصرت وقربت ہے تو آبا ، بدرجہ اولی داخل ہوں گے۔
- قاتل کے ساتھ دوسروں کو ملانے کی ضرورت اس لئے پیش آتی ہے تاکہ قاتل پر تخفیف ہو اور عاقلہ پر بھی تخفیف ہو۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اس بات کا لحاظ رکھا گیا ہے کہ کسی سے تین یا چار درہم سے زیادہ نہ لئے جائیں۔
اور جرح کو دور کرنا اس وقت ہوسکتا ہے جب ان میں تکثر ہو جن کو ملایا جارہا ہے اور آباء اور ابناء، عادۃ اتنے نہیں ہوتے کہ ان میں کثرت ہو اور وہ ادا و دیت کے لئے کافی ہو جائیں۔
As for the fathers and sons, it is said they are included due to their closeness, and it is said they are not included because the annexation is to remove hardship so that each one does not receive more than three or four (dirhams), and this meaning only materializes when there is multiplicity, and fathers and sons are not numerous. Commentary: There is a question whether the killer's fathers and his sons are included in the list of 'aqila. There are two opinions. If the basis of being 'aqila is assistance and closeness, then fathers are a fortiori included. The need to include others with the killer arises to alleviate burden on the killer and on the 'aqila. This is why it is observed that no one is charged more than three or four dirhams. And removal of hardship can only occur when those being annexed are numerous, and fathers and sons are usually not so numerous as to be sufficient for payment of diyah.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage discusses an internal Hanafi dispute regarding whether the killer's own father and sons are counted among the 'aqila. One opinion includes them because of their closeness in lineage; the 'aqila is based on support and closeness, so the father and sons are the closest. The other opinion excludes them because the purpose of the 'aqila is to alleviate hardship by distributing the payment among many people. Since fathers and sons are few in number, including them would not achieve the desired alleviation; in fact, it might place a heavy burden on them. The commentator explains both views without giving a preference, leaving the matter as a recognized difference.

Key Terms
آباء (aba'): The killer's male ascendants (father, grandfather, etc.).
أبناء (abna'): The killer's male descendants (sons, grandsons, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the 'aqila is only composed of the 'asabah

Key Takeaway
The inclusion of the killer's father and sons in the 'aqila is a legitimate intra-Hanafi dispute, with one view emphasising closeness and the other emphasising multiplicity as the operative rationale.

Extending 'Aqila to Military Companies (Rayat)
Extends the 'aqila ruling to military companies (rayat).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on extending the 'aqila system to military companies (rayat) and identify the role of the imam in determining proximity.

Core Idea
Hanafi law extends the 'aqila system to military companies, with the imam determining closeness by support, not lineage.

This lesson builds on the previous ruling regarding the 'aqila (blood money paying group) when one tribe is insufficient. The Hanafi school applies the same principle to military companies (rayat) in an army. If one company cannot pay the diyah, the closest company in terms of mutual support is added, following the 'closest then next closest' order. The imam is entrusted with determining this proximity because he knows the relationships between units.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling on 'aqila
Recall that when one tribe cannot pay diyah, the closest tribe in lineage is annexed. This is the basis for the extension.
2
Recognize the new case: military companies (rayat)
Understand that the same principle applies to army units rather than tribes. The text explicitly says 'upon this is the ruling of the companies'.
Rayat literally means banners; here it denotes organized military groups.
3
Determine the criterion for closeness
For tribes, closeness is based on lineage; for companies, it is based on mutual support (nusra). This is a shift in the effective cause (illa) for the analogy.
The text states 'closest in support' (اقربهم نصرة).
4
Identify the authority for determination
The imam decides which company is closest in support. The text delegates this to him because he is the 'knower of it' (العالم به).
This recognizes the imam's superior knowledge of military relations.
5
Confirm the Hanafi exclusivity
Note that this extension is specific to the Hanafi school. Other schools, like the Shafi'i, do not recognize organized groups as 'aqila and require equal payment per person.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the student should understand both views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا حكم الرايات اذا لم يتسع لذلك اهل راية ضم اليهم اقرب الرايا يعني اقربهم نصرة اذا حزبهم امر الاقرب فالاقرب ويفوض ذلك الى الامام لانه هو العالم به ثم هذا كله عندنا
ترجمہ اور اسی طریقہ پر رایات کا حکم ہے جب کہ اس کے لئے ایک جھنڈے والے ناکافی ہوں تو ان کی اقرب الرایات کو ملا دیا جائے گا یعنی ان میں سب سے زیادہ قریب ہوں نصرت کے اعتبار سے جب کہ ان کو کوئی امر پیش آ جائے الا قرب فالاقرب کے لحاظ سے اور اس کو امام کے سپر د کر دیا جائے اس لئے کہ اس بات کو وہی جانتا ہے۔ پھر یہ ساری تفصیل ہمارے نزدیک ہیں۔ تشریح اگر یہی صورت لشکر کی کمپنیوں میں ہوگئی ہو تو ایک کمپنی یا ایک رجسٹر میں جن کا نام درج ہے وہ اداء دیت کے لئے ناکافی ہیں تو انکی طرف اس دوسری کمپنی کو ملا دیا جائے گا جو ان کے نصرت و مدد کے لحاظ سے قریب ہو اور یہی الا قرب فالا قرب کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے آگے بھی ملایا جا سکتا ہے اور چونکہ ان امور سے امام واقف ہے اس لئے اس کو امام کے حوالہ کر دیا جائے گا بہر حال تفصیلات مذکورہ حنفیہ کے مسلک کے مطابق ہیں
And upon this is the ruling of the companies (rayat). If the people of one company are not sufficient for that, then the closest of the companies are annexed to them, meaning the closest in support (nusra) when an incident befalls them, the closest then the next closest, and that is delegated to the imam because he is the knower of it. Then all this is according to us (Hanafis). Commentary: If the same situation occurs in army companies, and one company or register whose names are recorded is insufficient for payment of diyah, then another company that is closer in support and assistance is annexed to them, and this consideration of closest then next closest may be applied further. And since the imam is aware of these matters, it is delegated to him. In any case, the details mentioned are according to the Hanafi school.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling on tribes to military companies (rayat). The same principle applies: if the members of one company are insufficient to pay the diyah, the next closest company in terms of support (nusra) is added, following the same 'closest then next closest' order. Unlike tribes, where lineage determines closeness, here closeness is based on mutual support and proximity in military organization. The determination of which company is closest is left to the imam, as he is best informed about the relationships between companies. The passage concludes by affirming that this is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
رایات (rayat): Military companies or regiments, literally 'banners' or 'flags'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Contribution Amount in 'Aqila
Presents the Shafi'i view of equal half-dinar contribution and the Hanafi rebuttal based on rank difference with zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school allows the contribution amount in 'aqila to be less than half a dinar and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on qiyas to zakat.

Core Idea
Diyah is lower in rank than zakat because it is not taken from principal wealth, allowing greater alleviation.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the minimum contribution each member of the 'aqila must pay when sharing the diyah. The Shafi'i view, based on analogy to zakat, requires each member to pay at least half a dinar. The Hanafi school argues that diyah is lower in rank than zakat, permitting a lower amount to maximize relief for the contributors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the Hanafi ruling on the minimum contribution amount. The Hanafi school allows an amount less than half a dinar (e.g., 3-4 dirhams) to achieve greater alleviation.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that each member must pay exactly half a dinar. His proof is that diyah is a gift (sila) like zakat, so it should be analogized to zakat, whose minimum payment is half a dinar.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts by pointing out that diyah is not taken from the principal wealth, proving it is lower in rank than zakat. Therefore, the analogy does not hold, and a lower amount is permissible.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In a case with many 'aqila members, the Shafi'i view fixes each obligation at half a dinar regardless of number, while the Hanafi view allows distribution with lower per-person amounts, easing the burden.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند الشافعي يجب على كل واحد نصف دينار فيسوى بين الكل لانه صلة فيعتبر بالزكواة وادناها ذلك ال خمسة دراهم عندهم نصف دينار ولكنا نقول هى احط رتبة منها الاترى انه لا تؤخذ من اصل المال فينتقص منها تحقيقا لزيادة التخفيف
ترجمہ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ہر ایک کے اوپر آدھا دینا واجب ہے پس تمام کے درمیان برابری کی جائے گی اس لئے کہ یہ صلہ ہے تو اس کو ز کوۃ پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور زکوۃ کی ادنی مقدار نصف دینا ر ہے اس لئے کہ صحابہ کے نزدیک پانچ درا ہم آدھا دینار ہے لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ دیت رتبہ کے اعتبار سے زکوۃ سے کم ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ دیت اصل مال سے نہیں لی جاتی پس دیت زکوۃ سے کم ہو گی تخفیف کی زیادتی کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے۔ تشریح امام شافعی کے نزدیک کم سے کم مقدار پانچ در اہم یا آدھا دینار عاقلہ میں سے ہر ایک پر واجب کیا جائے گا اور اس میں عاقلہ کے تمام افراد مساوی ہوں گے خواہ باپ ہو یا بیٹا یا اس کے علاوہ کوئی اور ہو۔
اور ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جیسے زکوۃ ایک صلہ ہے یعنی بغیر کسی عوض کے زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے اسی طرح دیت بھی ایک صلہ ہے لہذا دیت کو زکوۃ پر قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ اور زکوۃ کا اقل نصاب دو سو در اہم ہے جس میں زکوۃ کے پانچ در اہم واجب ہونگے۔ تو اسی طرح دیت میں بھی کم سے کم ہر ایک پر پانچ درا ہم واجب ہوں گے یا نصف دینار واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ نصف دینار پانچ دراہم کی قیمت صحابہ کے دور میں برابر تھی۔
According to al-Shafi'i, half a dinar is obligatory on each one, so he equalizes between all because it is a gift (sila) and thus it is analogized to zakat, and the minimum of that is five dirhams, which according to them is half a dinar. But we (Hanafis) say: it is lower in rank than it. Do you not see that it is not taken from the principal wealth? So it is less than zakat, in order to achieve greater alleviation. Commentary: According to Imam Shafi'i, the minimum amount of five dirhams or half a dinar is obligatory on each member of the 'aqila, and all members are equal, whether father, son, or anyone else. Their evidence is that just as zakat is a gift (sila) without compensation, so too diyah is a gift, so diyah is analogized to zakat. The minimum nisab of zakat is two hundred dirhams, from which five dirhams are due. Similarly, in diyah, each person must pay at least five dirhams or half a dinar, because half a dinar was equivalent to five dirhams in the time of the Companions.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents a cross-madhhab dispute on the minimum amount each member of the 'aqila must pay. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since diyah is a 'sila' (gift/compensation without exchange), it is analogous to zakat. The minimum zakat payment on 200 dirhams is 5 dirhams (or half a dinar), so each 'aqila member should pay exactly that amount equally. The Hanafi response is that diyah is actually lower in rank than zakat. Evidence: zakat is taken from a person's principal wealth (al-mal al-asli), while diyah contributions are not taken from the principal wealth but from distributed liability. Therefore, diyah allows for greater alleviation (takhfif), and the Hanafi school allows amounts less than half a dinar (e.g., three or four dirhams) depending on the number of members. The Hanafi view prioritizes distributional equity over formal analogy to zakat.

Key Terms
صلہ (sila): A gift or compensation given without expectation of return; both zakat and diyah are classified as sila.
احط رتبة (ahuttu rutbah): Lower in rank or status; Hanafi argues diyah is lower than zakat in legal hierarchy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school argue that diyah contributions can be less than the zakat minimum?
A) Because diyah is not a gift (sila)
B) Because diyah is taken from the principal wealth
C) Because diyah is not taken from principal wealth, so it is lower in rank than zakat
D) Because the Shafi'i school demands more

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows the 'aqila contribution to be less than the zakat minimum because diyah is not taken from principal wealth, prioritizing alleviation over strict analogy to zakat.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Minimum 'Aqila Contribution: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on Half Dinar vs. 3–4 Dirhams
Inter-madhhab dispute on minimum 'aqila contribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum diyah contribution per 'aqila member, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the distinction between zakah and diyah.

Core Idea
Diyah is lower than zakah; its minimum per person is 3–4 dirhams, not half a dinar.

The obligation of diyah (blood money) falls upon the 'aqila (the kin group) when a member commits homicide or causes injury. A key question is the minimum amount each member must contribute. This passage presents the Shafi'i analogy to zakah (both are gratuitous payments) and the Hanafi rebuttal, emphasizing that diyah's lesser rank warrants a lower amount.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the minimum contribution per 'aqila member according to Imam al-Shafi'i (half dinar or 5 dirhams) and the Hanafi school (3 or 4 dirhams).
Both agree that the 'aqila collectively pays, but differ on the individual minimum.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i analogy
Understand the Shafi'i dalil: diyah and zakah are both 'sila' (gratuitous payments), so diyah should be analogized to zakah. The minimum zakah on nisab (200 dirhams) is 5 dirhams/half dinar.
The analogy relies on the common attribute (sila).
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy because zakah is taken from original wealth (asl al-mal), whereas diyah is not. Diyah is of lower rank, so greater leniency requires a lower minimum.
The illa (effective cause) of zakah includes wealth, which is absent in diyah.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: the minimum contribution differs by about 1–2 dirhams per person, affecting the total burden on the 'aqila.
This difference can be significant in large 'aqila groups.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position (3–4 dirhams) is the relied-upon ruling in the madhhab, as stated in Ashraf al-Hidaya.
Later Hanafi authorities maintain this view.

And their proof is that just as zakah is a gratuitous payment (i.e., without compensation), similarly diyah is also a gratuitous payment, so diyah is analogized to zakah. And the minimum nisab of zakah is two hundred dirhams, upon which five dirhams are obligatory. So similarly in diyah, the minimum upon each person is five dirhams or half a dinar, because half a dinar was equivalent to five dirhams in the era of the Companions. Our proof is that the rank of zakah is higher than diyah because zakah is obligatory on the original wealth, while diyah is not obligatory on the original wealth but rather on the 'sila' (gratuitous payment). So it is known that the rank of diyah is lower than zakah. Therefore, its amount must be less than zakah so that it is known that its rank is lower and that there is greater alleviation in it. Hence, we have adopted the opinion of three or four dirhams, reducing from five.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the minimum amount each member of the 'aqila must contribute toward diyah. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since diyah, like zakah, is a gratuitous payment (sila) from the state treasury, it should be analogized to zakah. The minimum zakah payment from the nisab of 200 dirhams is 5 dirhams (or half a dinar). Therefore, each member should pay at least half a dinar or 5 dirhams. The Hanafi school responds that diyah is of a lower rank than zakah. The evidence is that zakah is taken directly from the original wealth (asl al-mal), whereas diyah is not; it is taken from the 'aqila's payments. Because of this greater leniency, the amount should be less. Hence, Hanafis hold that the minimum is 3 or 4 dirhams, not 5. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) considering the purpose of relief. The dispute centers on the correct analogy (qiyas) and the evaluation of the 'illa (effective cause): Shafi'is focus on the generic similarity (both are gratuitous payments), while Hanafis consider the specific difference in obligation (zakah is on wealth, diyah is on persons).

Key Terms
صلة (sila): A gratuitous payment without compensation, used to describe both zakah and diyah in their nature.
دية (diya): Blood money paid for homicide or injury.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakah obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because zakah is taken from original wealth, whereas diyah is not.
C) Because the minimum of zakah is actually 2.5%.
D) Because the 'aqila is not analogous to a zakah payer.

Key Takeaway
The minimum diyah contribution per 'aqila member is 3–4 dirhams in the Hanafi school, derived from the principle that diyah's lesser rank than zakah demands greater leniency.

Diyat — Blood Money

Proof of Diyah's Lower Status and Payment from Stipends
Proof of diyah's lower status and ruling on payment from stipends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why diyah is reduced compared to zakat and state how diyah is paid from stipends when the 'aqila are stipend recipients.

Core Idea
Diyah is paid from stipends over three years because it is lower in rank than zakat and must be adjusted proportionally to stipend frequency.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary establishes a key principle: diyah's status is lower than zakat, justifying its reduced amount. It then applies this principle to a specific scenario: when the 'aqila are stipend recipients rather than annual grant recipients. The ruling details how diyah is collected proportionally over three years, with the amount taken per stipend depending on its payment schedule.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the comparative proof
The author first proves diyah's lower status by comparing it to zakat: zakat is wajib on principal wealth, while diyah is not. This analogy establishes that diyah's amount must be less than zakat's, justifying the reduction from five to three or four dirhams.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on hierarchical comparison.
2
Identify the key analogy for stipends
The passage then analogizes the regular stipend (rizq) to the annual grant (ata) because both are gifts from the treasury. This analogy extends the same payment rule: diyah is taken from stipends over three years, one-third each year.
The analogy uses the illa of 'both being treasury gifts'.
3
Apply the frequency rule
The proportion deducted from each stipend depends on how often it is paid: if annual, take 1/3; if semi-annual, take 1/6; if monthly, take 1/36 of the total diyah per stipend, ensuring that the annual total equals one-third of diyah.
This ensures that over three years the full diyah is collected.
4
Integrate the three-year time frame
The entire payment is spread over three years, with one-third collected each year. The frequency rule ensures that the annual collection matches exactly one-third, regardless of whether stipends are paid annually, semi-annually, or monthly.
The time frame is consistent with the general rule for 'aqila payment from grants.

Our proof is that the status of zakat is higher than diyah because zakat is obligatory on the original wealth while diyah is not obligatory on the original wealth but is obligatory on the 'silat'. Therefore it is known that the rank of diyah is lower than zakat. So its amount must be reduced from zakat so that it may be known that its rank is lower than zakat and it has more reduction than zakat. Hence we have adopted the opinion of reducing from five to three or four dirhams. If the killer is from among the ashab al-arzaq (stipend recipients) instead of ahl al-ata', then diyah will be upon the ahl al-arzaq. And if the 'aqila of the man are ashab al-arzaq, diyah is decreed against their stipends over three years, one-third each year, because for them the stipend (rizq) is in the place of 'ata' and stands in its position, since each of them is a gift from the treasury. Then it is considered: if their stipends come out every year, then just as a stipend is given, one-third is taken from it similar to 'ata'. And if it comes out every six months, and it comes after the decree, one-sixth of the diyah is taken from it. And if it comes out every month, from each stipend its share of the month is taken, so that the total taken in each year equals one-third. And if it comes out a day or more after the decree, from that month's stipend the share of the month is taken. Translation: And if the man's (the killer's) people are stipend recipients, then the payment of diyah is decreed against their stipends over three years, each year one-third, because for them the stipend is in the rank of 'ata' and stands in its place, since each is a gift from the treasury. Then it is seen: if their stipends come out annually, then from what comes out, one-third is taken in the rank of 'ata'. And if the stipend comes out semi-annually and comes after the decree, then one-sixth of diyah is taken from it. And if it comes monthly, then from each stipend the share of the month is taken until the total collected in a year equals one-third. And if the stipend comes out a day or more after the decree, then from that month's stipend the share of the month is taken. Explanation: 'Ata' is what the people of the register receive as annual reward. There are different opinions about the interpretation of rizq: (1) What poor people receive from the treasury due to their poverty is called rizq. (2) What soldiers receive for monthly necessities is called rizq, and there are opinions. In brief, the author intends to say that if the killer is not from ahl al-ata' but from ashab al-arzaq, then rizq stands in the place of 'ata'. Therefore, now the diyah will be decreed against the stipends, which will be collected over three years, and annually one-third will be collected. Then if the stipend from the treasury comes annually, this is the calculation; if it comes every six months, whenever it comes, one-sixth will be taken from it so that in one year it becomes one-third; and if the stipend comes monthly, then every month [؟] will be taken so that in one year it becomes one-third. The rest of the text is easy.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the payment of diyah when the 'aqila (the group liable for blood money) are recipients of regular stipends (rizq) from the state treasury, as opposed to annual grants ('ata). The passage first establishes a foundational proof: zakat has a higher status than diyah because zakat is obligatory on the principal wealth itself, whereas diyah is not obligatory on principal wealth but on the 'silat' (likely a type of payment). Therefore, diyah's amount is reduced to reflect its lower status. The author adopts the view that diyah is reduced from five to three or four dirhams. Then comes the main ruling: if the killer belongs to the class of stipend recipients (ashab al-arzaq) rather than grant recipients (ahl al-ata'), diyah is imposed on the stipends. The 'aqila's stipends are used to pay diyah over three years, one-third each year, because for them the stipend is analogous to the grant given to others. The method of deduction depends on how often the stipend is paid: if annually, one-third of each annual stipend is taken; if semi-annually, one-sixth of each stipend; if monthly, a proportionate share each month such that the yearly total equals one-third. If the stipend is disbursed after the judge's decree, the same proportional rule applies. The Urdu tashreeh (explanation) clarifies that 'ata is an annual reward for those enrolled in the military register, while rizq is either a stipend for the poor or a monthly allowance for soldiers. The summary reiterates that when the killer is from stipend recipients, diyah is collected from their stipends over three years, with the proportion determined by the frequency of payment.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid by the 'aqila (or killer) to the heirs of a victim of unintentional homicide.
عاقلہ ('aqila): The group liable to pay diyah on behalf of the killer, typically the 'asabah (agnatic relatives) or the state treasury for those without such relatives.
رزق (rizq): A regular stipend or allowance from the state treasury, often given to soldiers or the poor monthly or semi-annually.
عطاء ('ata'): An annual grant or reward given by the state to those enrolled in the diwan (military register).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How is diyah collected from the 'aqila who receive semi-annual stipends?
A) One-third of each semi-annual stipend is taken for one year.
B) One-sixth of each semi-annual stipend is taken, so that the annual total equals one-third of diyah.
C) Half of each semi-annual stipend is taken.
D) The full diyah is taken from the first stipend.

Key Takeaway
Diyah is wajib on the 'aqila and is paid from stipends over three years, one-third each year, with proportional deduction based on stipend frequency.

Diyah Collection from Annual Grants vs Monthly Stipends
Ruling on diyah source when 'āqila receive both monthly stipends and annual grants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on which source of income diyah is taken from when the 'āqila receive both monthly stipends and annual grants, and explain the legal reasoning based on ease and avoidance of hardship.

Core Idea
Diyah is taken from surplus annual grants, not subsistence stipends, to avoid hardship.

This passage addresses a practical fiqh scenario: when the 'āqila (the killer's relatives responsible for paying diyah) receive both a regular monthly stipend (rizq) and an annual grant ('aṭiyah) from the state treasury. The ruling determines which of these two sources should be used to pay the diyah. Understanding this ruling illustrates how Hanafi fiqh prioritizes ease and prevents hardship in financial obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage carefully. It describes a situation where the 'āqila have two forms of state income: a monthly stipend (rizq) and an annual grant ('aṭiyah). Note the key terms.
The Arabic uses 'arzāq' (plural of rizq) and 'aṭīyāt' (plural of 'aṭiyah).
2
State the ruling
The passage clearly states that the diyah is imposed on the annual grants, not on the monthly stipends. This is the definitive legal ruling.
The ruling is wajib: it is obligatory to collect from the grants first.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The text gives three possible reasons: grants are larger (more abundant), stipends are for daily sufficiency (so taking would be difficult), and grants are for maintaining the army for support (so they are surplus). Identify which reason primarily drives the ruling.
The underlying principle is 'raf' al-haraj' (removing hardship).
4
Apply the principle to similar cases
Consider if the 'āqila have other sources of wealth (e.g., savings, property). The principle of choosing the least burdensome source may extend analogically.
This is a case of ta'lil (giving a reason) that can guide future applications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانت لهم ارزاق في كل شهر و اعطية في كل سنة فرضت الدية فى الاعطية دون الارزاق لانه ايسر أمالان الاعطية أكثر أولان الرزق لكفاية الوقت فيتعسر الاداء منه والعطيات ليكونوا في الديوان قائمين بالنصرة فيتيسر عليهم

ترجمہ اور اگر ان کے لئے ماہانہ ارزاق ہوں اور سالانہ عطیات ہوں تو دیت عطیات میں فرض کی جائے گی نہ کہ ارزاق میں اس لئے کہ یہ آسان ہے یا تو اس لئے کہ عطیات زیادہ ہیں یا اس لئے کہ رزق وقت کی کفایت کے لئے ہے تو اس میں سے ادا ئیگی مشکل ہے اور عطیات اس لئے ہیں کہ وہ دیوان میں نصرت پر قائم رہیں تو ان پر ادا نبیسگی آسان ہوگی ۔

تشریح اور اگر قاتل کے عاقلہ ایسے ہوں کہ ان کو بیت المال سے ماہانہ رزق بھی ملتا ہے اور سالا نہ عطایا بھی ہوتی ہیں تو دیت عطا یا میں سے وصول کی جائے گی اس لئے کہ ان کو اسی میں سہولت ہے کیونکہ عطا یا زیادہ ہوتی ہیں تو ان میں سے دیت دینا آسان ہوگا، نیز رزق بقدر کفایت ملتا ہے تو اس میں سے دیت دینا بھاری پڑیگا ۔
اور عطا یا اس لئے ہوتی ہیں کہ یہ مستقل فوج ہے ان کو اس لئے رکھا گیا ہے کہ بوقت ضرورت نصرت کا کام انجام دیں تو یہ مال ان کی روز مرہ کی حاجات سے زیادہ ہے تو اس میں سے ادا ئیگی آنسان ہے۔
And if they have monthly stipends (arzāq) and annual grants ('aṭīyāt), then the diyah is imposed on the grants, not on the stipends, because it is easier. Either because the grants are more, or because the stipend is for the sufficiency of the time, so payment from it would be difficult, and the grants are for them to remain in the register for support, so payment from them is easy. Translation: And if they have monthly stipends and annual grants, then diyah is made obligatory on the grants, not on the stipends, because this is easier, either because grants are more, or because the stipend is for daily sufficiency, so paying from it would be difficult, and grants are because they are in the register for rendering support, so paying from it will be easy. Explanation: And if the 'aqila of the killer are such that they receive both monthly stipend and annual grants from the treasury, then diyah will be collected from the grants, because it is easier for them, since grants are more, so paying diyah from them will be easy. Also, the stipend is given just for sufficiency, so paying diyah from it would be burdensome. And grants are given because these are the standing army; they are kept to perform support when needed, so this wealth is more than their daily needs, so payment from it is easy.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling: when the 'aqila receive both monthly stipends (rizq) and annual grants ('ata'), the diyah is imposed solely on the annual grants, not on the monthly stipends. The reasoning provided is practicality: grants are larger and meant for purposes beyond daily subsistence (like military readiness), so paying diyah from them is easier and does not disrupt the recipient's essential needs. The stipend, however, is just enough for daily living, so taking diyah from it would cause hardship. The Urdu tashreeh reinforces this: grants are more substantial and are intended for the standing army's support, making them the appropriate source for diyah payments. This ruling is a clear application of the Hanafi principle of avoiding hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Key Terms
عطیہ ('aṭiyah): Annual grant given by the state to those enrolled in the diwan, typically soldiers.
رزق (rizq): Monthly stipend or livelihood allowance provided to meet daily needs.
دية (diyah): Blood money; financial compensation paid to the heirs of a victim in cases of homicide or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage
